26th Executive Yuan National Affairs Meeting 22

Chen Qicai of the Jiangsu Finance Department Resigns, Xu Baoying Succeeds

Temporary Regulations for Exchange Supervisors Passed

The Executive Yuan held its 26th National Affairs Meeting on the 16th. Those present included Song Ziwen, Liu Shangqing, Liu Ruiheng, Ma Fuxiang, Wang Zhengting, Lian Shenghai, and Kong Xiangxi. Those attending as observers included Chen Yi, Wei Yichang, Li Shuhua, and Chen Shaokuan. Vice President Song Ziwen chaired the meeting. There were 31 items reported and 18 items discussed. The following are the items recorded for publication: (A) Reported Items: (1) The Political Affairs Office submitted four proposals from the National Assembly sent to the Executive Yuan by the Civil Affairs Bureau of the National Government for handling, with a note stating the proposed handling by the Executive Yuan for review; (2) The Ministry of Industry submitted the draft regulations for the inspection of imported silkworm eggs by the Commodity Inspection Bureau for review and record; (3) He Chengjun, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, Liu Wendao, Member and Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Wu Guozhen, Member and Director of the Finance Department, Fang Dazhi, Member and Director of the Construction Department, Huang Jianzhong, Member and Director of the Education Department, Peng Jieshi, Member and Secretary-General, Ma Dengjun, Zhu Huaibing, Chen Guangzu, and others, telegraphed that they were sworn into office on the 10th for inspection; (4) Various ministries, commissions, provincial governments, and municipal governments submitted 25 work reports; (B) Items for Discussion: (1) The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry jointly presented 13 articles of the draft temporary regulations for exchange supervisors for review and instructions. The resolution was passed; (2) The Ministry of Industry presented the temporary organizational rules of the Qingdao Agricultural and Forestry Office, which were submitted for review and discussion. After deliberation and revision, the revised draft was submitted for review and implementation. The resolution was passed with revisions; (3) The Anti-Smoking Committee submitted the revised charter of the Capital Anti-Smoking Hospital for review and implementation. The resolution was approved; (4) The resolution was made to approve the resignation of Chen Qicai, Member and Director of the Finance Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and to transfer the request for approval, and to appoint Xu Baoying as the successor to the position of Member and Director of the Finance Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government; (5) The resolution was made to approve the resignation of Yang Mianzhong, Member and Secretary-General of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, from the concurrent position of Secretary-General, and to transfer the request for approval, and to appoint Zhou Jietao as the successor to fill the vacancy.

Sino-Polish Treaty of Amity and Commerce 23

The Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation between China and Poland has been ratified by both countries and is hereby promulgated as follows:

The Republic of China and the Republic of Poland, in order to promote friendly relations between the two countries, develop mutual commerce, and benefit the people of both countries, have decided to conclude a Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation based on the principles of equality, reciprocity, and mutual respect for sovereignty. To this end, they have appointed as their Plenipotentiaries: The Chairman of the National Government of the Republic of China, His Excellency Wang Zhengting, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government of the Republic of China; The President of the Republic of Poland, His Excellency Włodzimierz Drymmer, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the Republic of Poland to China. The aforementioned Plenipotentiaries, after having communicated to each other their full powers, found in good and due form, have resolved to agree upon the following articles:

Article 1. There shall be perpetual peace and amity between the Republic of China and the Republic of Poland and between their peoples.

Article 2. Each of the High Contracting Parties shall have the right to send duly accredited diplomatic representatives to the other. Such representatives shall reciprocally enjoy in the country to which they are accredited all the treatment, rights, privileges, and immunities recognized by international law.

Article 3. Each of the High Contracting Parties may appoint Consuls-General, Consuls, Vice-Consuls, and Consular Agents to reside in the territories of the other, in such places as may be agreed upon. Such consular officers shall reciprocally enjoy the same privileges and treatment as those of other countries and shall be entitled to exercise the functions which are recognized by international usage. The local authorities of each country shall give to the consular officers of the other such assistance as may be required for the due exercise of their functions. Before assuming their duties, all consular officers shall, in accordance with international practice, obtain from the government of the country to which they are sent an exequatur which may be withdrawn by the said government should it consider necessary to do so. The two governments shall not appoint persons engaged in commerce or industry in the country to which they are sent as consular officers, with the exception of honorary consuls.

Article 4. The nationals of each of the High Contracting Parties shall have liberty to enter the territory of the other provided that they are furnished with passports issued by the competent authorities of their country, certifying their nationality and the object of their journey, and duly visaed by the consular officers of the country to which they are proceeding. The fees for such visas shall be based on the principle of reciprocity.

Article 5. The nationals of each of the High Contracting Parties shall be entitled to receive in the territory of the other the most constant protection and security for their persons and property, and shall enjoy in that respect the same rights and privileges as are or may be granted to nationals of any other country, or to native nationals. In particular, they shall have the right to travel, reside, study, work, trade, and engage in any legitimate enterprise or occupation in any place where the nationals of any other country are or may be permitted to do so, subject to the local laws and regulations. They shall pay no other or higher taxes than are or may be levied on nationals of the country.

Article 6. The nationals of each of the High Contracting Parties shall be subject to the laws and jurisdiction of the local courts of the country where they reside in all matters of civil and criminal litigation. They shall have the right to sue and defend their rights in the local courts and shall be entitled to the same freedom in the choice of lawyers and agents as the nationals of the country.

Article 7. Neither of the High Contracting Parties shall compel the nationals of the other to serve in its military or naval forces, or to pay any taxes or contributions in lieu thereof, or to perform any compulsory labor or services, or to subscribe to any public loan or donation.

Article 8. The nationals of each of the High Contracting Parties shall, in the territory of the other, be subject to the following provisions with respect to their property and estates: (1) They shall have the right to dispose freely of their property, to export it freely, to remit it freely, and to make wills freely disposing of it. (2) The laws of the country of the deceased shall govern matters of inheritance, but the laws of the place where the property is located shall govern all public law restrictions on the whole or part of the inheritance. (3) Nationals of each High Contracting Party shall have the right to inherit property in the territory of the other, whether or not there is a will. If the deceased has no legal heirs or administrators under the laws of his country, and has not disposed of his property by will, the property shall be taken care of and disposed of by the consul of the country of the deceased in accordance with the laws of his country. The same shall apply if nationals of one High Contracting Party have property in the territory of the other but die outside that country, and there are no legal heirs or administrators in the place where the property is located. (4) If a national of one High Contracting Party dies at sea, the property he was carrying shall be delivered to the nearest consul of the country of the deceased. (5) The taxes, fees, and charges levied on such inheritance shall not be higher or different from those levied on nationals of the country in similar circumstances.

Article 9. The governments of each of the High Contracting Parties shall not search or inspect the public houses, private residences, warehouses, shops, and all appurtenances used for business purposes, as well as commercial account books, commercial correspondence, and all objects of use, of the nationals of the other in their respective territories, except in accordance with the express provisions of the law.

Article 10. It is agreed between the High Contracting Parties that matters relating to customs duties shall be entirely regulated by the domestic laws of each country. It is further agreed that, in respect of customs duties and related matters, each High Contracting Party shall enjoy in the territory of the other the same treatment as is or may be granted to any other country. Neither High Contracting Party shall, on any pretext, levy on the import or export of goods belonging to the nationals of the other country higher or different customs duties, internal taxes, or any other taxes than those levied on its own nationals or on the nationals of any other country.

Article 11. The governments of each of the High Contracting Parties shall not establish any prohibitions or restrictions on the import, export, or transit of raw or manufactured goods produced in their respective territories, which do not apply to the same goods imported from, exported to, or transited through any third country. The governments of both countries may independently determine prohibitions or restrictions on imports, exports, and transit relating to national defense, civilian food supply, public safety, sanitation, prevention of animal diseases, cultural relics, and state monopolies.

Article 12. The governments of each of the High Contracting Parties shall protect the trademarks and designs used by the nationals of the other Party which have been duly registered with the competent authorities of the country where they are used.

Article 13. Commercial companies organized under the laws of either of the High Contracting Parties shall be permitted to establish businesses in the territory of the other Party in accordance with the procedures stipulated by the laws of the country where they are located, to operate within the scope of the laws of the country where they are located, and to engage in their business activities. All provisions of Articles 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, and 12 of this Treaty shall apply equally to such companies, except for those provisions which by their nature can only apply to individuals.

Article 14. Each of the High Contracting Parties reserves to itself the right to regulate navigation on its internal waterways and coastal trade for its own nationals.

Article 15. For the purpose of this Treaty, all vessels recognized as Chinese vessels under Chinese law and all vessels recognized as Polish vessels under Polish law shall be deemed to be Chinese or Polish vessels respectively. Each of the High Contracting Parties agrees to allow merchant vessels of the other Party to freely enter all coastal ports that have been opened for trade, to anchor, and to load and unload passengers and cargo, within the scope of current laws and regulations. These merchant vessels shall fully comply with all regulations of the respective ports. Polish vessels in Chinese ports and Chinese vessels in Polish ports, if they fully comply with the obligations stipulated by laws and customs or port regulations and do not violate any prohibitions, shall not be detained or arrested, nor shall their cargo or materials, except in accordance with legal procedures.

Article 16. If merchant vessels of either of the High Contracting Parties are wrecked, run aground, or encounter other dangers in the coastal areas of the other Party, they may enter any port or harbor of the other Party, even if it has not been opened, for refuge. The local authorities shall notify the nearest consular office of the respective country and provide assistance in accordance with international practice. The merchant vessel may repair damages and purchase necessary supplies for export without paying additional port taxes. If the merchant vessel is forced to sell its cargo, it shall comply with the laws of the country where it is located and pay taxes. If the merchant vessel continues to trade in a port where trade is permitted by law, it shall pay taxes in accordance with regulations, even under the same circumstances.

Article 17. Warships and merchant vessels of either of the High Contracting Parties transporting troops or military supplies shall not enter the territorial waters, bays, and ports of the other Party without the special permission of the government of the other Party. If such vessels are wrecked, run aground, or encounter other dangers in the coastal areas of the other Party, the local authorities shall provide assistance in accordance with international practice.

Article 18. If internal disturbances occur on board a merchant vessel of either of the High Contracting Parties within the territorial waters of the other Party, and the local authorities deem that they endanger local security, the local authorities shall have jurisdiction to handle the matter.

Article 19. This Treaty shall be in effect for a period of three years from the date of its entry into force. Six months before the expiration of the term, either of the High Contracting Parties may give notice of amendment or termination. If neither party gives notice of amendment or termination by that time, the Treaty shall continue in effect. However, after the expiration of the term, either of the High Contracting Parties may give notice of amendment or termination at any time. This Treaty shall expire one year after the date of such notice.

Article 20. The Polish Government, being responsible for the conduct of the foreign relations of the Free City of Danzig, reserves the right to declare the Free City of Danzig as a party to this Treaty, recognizing the obligations arising from this Treaty and acquiring the rights arising from this Treaty.

Article 21. This Treaty is written in duplicate in Chinese, Polish, and French. In case of discrepancies in interpretation, the French text shall prevail.

Article 22. This Treaty shall be ratified by the High Contracting Parties in accordance with their respective fundamental laws. The instruments of ratification shall be exchanged at Nanking at the earliest possible date. This Treaty shall enter into force on the thirtieth day after the two governments have mutually notified each other of ratification. The aforementioned thirtieth day shall be calculated from the date of the last notification of ratification. In witness whereof, the Plenipotentiaries of the two countries have signed and sealed this Treaty to attest to its authenticity. Done at Nanking on the eighteenth day of September, the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the eighteenth day of September, one thousand nine hundred and twenty-nine of the Christian Era. Wang Zhengting [Seal] Włodzimierz Drymmer [Seal]

Protocol of Signature

The Plenipotentiaries of the Republic of China and the Republic of Poland, upon signing today's Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation between China and Poland, hereby mutually agree to declare as follows:

Declaration Document 1 (Regarding matters stipulated in Article 4 of this Treaty) (1) Before the conclusion of this Treaty, the passports of Poles residing in China shall be submitted to the local authorities for visaing after the conclusion of this Treaty to replace the residence permits previously issued by China to Poles residing in China. (2) Polish nationals in China who hold passports from their country visaed by the Chinese supervisory authorities may freely travel to any place where the nationals of any other country can travel without prior permission, without the need to request prior permission for each trip. Chinese nationals who hold passports visaed by the Polish supervisory authorities shall enjoy the same rights in Poland.

Declaration Document 2 (Regarding matters stipulated in Article 10 of this Treaty) The provisions of Article 10 shall not apply to any tax concessions that one Contracting Party now grants or may hereafter grant to contiguous countries to facilitate border trade, or to any preferential benefits arising from a customs union that one Contracting Party may hereafter conclude with another country, or to the special customs system between Polish Upper Silesia and German Upper Silesia.

Declaration Document 3 This Protocol shall be considered an integral part of today's Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation between China and Poland. In witness whereof, the Plenipotentiaries of the two countries have signed and sealed this Protocol to attest to its authenticity. Done at Nanking on the eighteenth day of September, the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the eighteenth day of September, one thousand nine hundred and twenty-nine of the Christian Era. Wang Zhengting [Seal] Włodzimierz Drymmer [Seal]

Annex

Note from the Polish Representative to the Chinese Representative: Regarding the matter of notification, the Polish churches and schools that have been established in China have always been given due protection by the local authorities of your country. Now that the relations between our two countries are becoming closer, the Government of my country is convinced that the local authorities of your country will continue to provide full protection to the churches and schools as before. As for the temples and schools of your country that are now or will be established in Poland, the Polish Government will provide the same protection in accordance with the Constitution of my country. I hereby notify you for your information. Włodzimierz Drymmer [Seal]

Note from the Chinese Representative to the Polish Representative: Regarding the matter of reply, your representative's notification of September 18th has been received, stating that the Polish churches and schools that have been established in China have always been given due protection by the local authorities of your country. Now that the relations between our two countries are becoming closer, the Government of my country is convinced that the local authorities of your country will continue to provide full protection to the churches and schools as before. As for the temples and schools of your country that are now or will be established in Poland, the Polish Government will provide the same protection in accordance with the Constitution of my country. I ask you to note the reply and inform us accordingly. I am pleased to learn that the local authorities of your country provide full protection to the temples and schools of our country that have been established in your country in accordance with the Constitution. The Government of my country will continue to provide the same protection to the churches and schools of your country that have already been established in China, within the scope of the laws and regulations of our country. I hereby notify you for your information. Wang Zhengting [Seal]

Supplementary Protocol to the Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation between China and Poland

The Plenipotentiaries of the Republic of China and the Republic of Poland, having been duly authorized by their respective governments, declare that the two parties agree to supplement and explain the provisions of the Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation signed on September 18th of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China as follows: (Article 4) The freedom to enter the territory of the other Contracting Party shall be subject to the scope of the domestic laws of that country, which shall apply to the nationals of all countries without any distinction. (Article 6) The local courts stipulated in Article 6, Libunaux Locaux, refer to the courts of that country which have jurisdiction in accordance with the current laws of the country where the litigant is located. (Article 8) Clause 1, the right to freely export property, shall be limited to not infringing on the domestic laws of the country. Clause 3, the granting of the right to inherit property, shall be limited to not exceeding the scope of the domestic laws of the country. (Article 10) and (Article 11) In order to ensure that both parties' commerce enjoys the benefits stipulated in Articles 10 and 11 of this Treaty, one of the Contracting Parties may require a certificate of origin to be attached to goods imported into its customs area. (Article 13) The two Contracting Parties mutually agree that foreign companies in each country may be required to obtain prior approval in accordance with the domestic laws of the country where they are located before they can be established. (Article 18) The two Contracting Parties mutually agree that the local authorities of one Contracting Party shall only interfere in matters occurring on vessels of the other Contracting Party at the request of the consul of the other Contracting Party or the shipowner, unless interference is necessary and delay would lead to serious consequences, or if non-crew members are involved in disturbances on the ship, in which case interference may be carried out without the aforementioned request. However, the interfering authorities shall immediately notify the nearest consul of the other Contracting Party of the facts. This Protocol, as part of the Treaty of Amity, Commerce, and Navigation signed on September 18th of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, shall be ratified within the shortest possible time, and the matters concerning the exchange of ratification documents, entry into force, validity period, and termination shall be handled in the same manner as the Treaty. In witness whereof, the Plenipotentiaries of the two countries have signed this Protocol to attest to its authenticity. This Protocol is written in duplicate and done at Nanking on the first day of July of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the first day of July, one thousand nine hundred and thirty of the Christian Era. Wang Zhengting [Seal] Włodzimierz Drymmer [Seal]

Case of Japanese Nationals Detained for Smuggling Qin and Han Dynasty Bricks and Tiles via the Jiaoji Railway 25

The Shandong Department of Education Sends Personnel to Verify the Situation

The Japanese Consul-General Strenuously Objects to Transportation to Jinan

The Port Authority Detains Another Batch of Antiquities

Negotiations Regarding Transportation from Qingdao to Jinan

Qingdao Dispatch: The previous report detailed the detention by the Qingdao station of the Jiaoji Railway of Japanese national Ota, who was privately selling all the Qin and Han dynasty bricks and tiles of the Gao family in Weixian for transport to Japan, and the dispatch of personnel by the Shandong Department of Education to Qingdao to negotiate the confiscation and transport measures. It is now learned that after Wu Jingshou, secretary of the Shandong Department of Education, arrived in Qingdao, he immediately contacted the Jiaoji Railway Bureau and the Municipal Government to discuss the confiscation and transportation methods, and also telegraphed both parties to request assistance in handling the matter. At 3:00 PM on the 12th, personnel from the Shandong Department of Education, the Jiaoji Railway Bureau, and the Municipal Government jointly dispatched personnel to open and inspect the sealed items. The Japanese Consulate and the antique dealer were also notified in advance to come to the site for verification. Those who attended on that day included Wu Jingshou from the Shandong Department of Education, Wen Shao from the Education Bureau, Li Zhaoyuan from the Social Affairs Bureau, Shi Runsheng from the Jiaoji Railway Party Department, Sui Jigu, Ma Guanwei, Zhang Yulin, Su Shoubin, and Fujita from the Jiaoji Railway Bureau, Tong Qingshan from the First Police Section, Zhou Shizhen, the stationmaster, Zhang Liangzuo from the Public Security Bureau, Pi Gaopin and Ding Botao from Qingdao University, and newspaper reporters. The Japanese side was represented by the Deputy Consul-General Hyakutake, Ueda Takayoshi, Shanxi Sidairo, and the antique dealer Ota. When the seal was opened, personnel from all parties were present to observe, but the Japanese personnel sat in the office and refused to come to the site for inspection. The Japanese Consul-General strenuously objected to the transportation of the antiquities to Jinan, stating that items purchased by private individuals with money should not be confiscated. Secretary Wu Jingshou replied that he was acting on the orders of the central government and that there was no confiscation, but only temporary custody, and that future handling would depend on the central government's instructions. After the debate, the inspection began. The first box contained 50 rectangular bricks and 7 small rectangular bricks, all with seal script inscriptions such as "May you be immortal for ten thousand generations" and "May you live a thousand autumns." The second box contained 9 large rectangular bricks and 143 small bricks, each with red edges. The inscriptions on the bricks varied, with some having nine characters, "May your descendants be secure, prosperous, and happy without end," and others having four characters, "Peace and happiness without end," "Limitless as the heavens," "Wei Zi tile count," and "Zhaoyang Palace Dang." The third box contained 175 packages of circular tile ends, each with the inscription "Prolong life and increase longevity." The fourth box contained 66 bricks of various sizes, all with inscriptions. The fifth box contained 89 bricks of various sizes, including square hollow bricks with patterns covering the entire surface, with ancient figures in the middle of the patterns. The sixth box was a long stone stele, engraved with two phoenixes. The seventh box was a rectangular broken stone tablet, which was not opened because it had been inspected the first time. After inspection, seals from the Department of Education, the Education Bureau, and the Social Affairs Bureau were affixed. Because the Japanese Deputy Consul-General was present, a seal from the Japanese Consulate-General in Qingdao was also affixed to the first box. Due to time constraints, only the number of items in each box was checked, and the names and dynasties of the bricks, tiles, and steles were not studied. However, according to experts in antique appraisal present at the scene, they were definitely precious Qin and Han dynasty antiquities. Although these antiquities have been inspected, they are still stored in the Qingdao station warehouse because the Japanese side does not allow them to be transported to Jinan. The Japanese Consulate in Qingdao has directly negotiated with the National Government on behalf of the Japanese merchant, and a decision on whether to confiscate all of them or pay a reasonable price will be made after the National Government's reply. Secretary Wu of the Shandong Department of Education has completed his mission and took the Jiaoji Railway train back to Jinan on the evening of the 13th to report everything to the Department of Education.

Yesterday, the Municipal Port Authority discovered another large batch of antiquities, totaling ten large boxes, at the Dagang Wharf. It is said that the foreign firm Meiji Trading Company purchased them from the interior of our country with the intention of shipping them abroad. Unexpectedly, when they were being loaded onto the ship, they were recognized by the personnel of the Port Authority's Surveillance Section, who immediately detained them and reported them to the Municipal Government for verification. The Municipal Government, considering that the items were related to Chinese culture, immediately approved the detention and decided that personnel from the Education Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau should be dispatched on the 15th to jointly open the boxes for inspection with the Port Authority, and then decide on how to deal with them. (June 13th)

Jinan Dispatch: After the Qin and Han dynasty bricks and tiles from Weixian were detained in Qingdao, the Shandong Department of Education, in order to preserve the antiquities, sent staff member Wu Jingshou to Qingdao to transport them to Jinan for safekeeping. After several twists and turns, the Jiaoji Railway Bureau received a telegram from the Ministry of Railways, which allowed them to be transported. After Wu Jingshou inspected them in Qingdao on the 12th, they were transported on the 13th. The Jiaoji Railway specially allocated a separate guard car for transportation and telegraphed all stations along the line to protect them properly. Unexpectedly, just as preparations were being made for loading on the morning of the 13th, the Japanese again strongly objected. The Japanese national Ota, who purchased the antiquities, had returned to Japan and entrusted Kuhara to transport them to Japan. Kuhara informed the Japanese Consul-General in Qingdao, who negotiated with our government officials on the one hand and informed Kagasaka Gaku (also a Japanese national, currently the Chief of the Traffic Department of the Jiaoji Railway) on the other hand, asking Ge Guangting, the Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, to prevent the start of transportation. The commotion lasted all day, and the planned arrival in Jinan on the 13th was changed. Finally, Wu Jingshou visited Ge Guangting, the Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, and earnestly stated that the transportation of the antiquities to Jinan for safekeeping was being carried out by the Department of Education on the orders of the Ministry of Education and by the Jiaoji Railway Bureau on the orders of the Ministry of Railways. Now, because of the Japanese obstruction, transportation could not begin. Was the Railway Bureau giving more weight to the orders of the Ministry or to the Japanese? It would be better to transport them to Jinan first and then negotiate with the Japanese. Ge agreed and discussed it with Kagasaka Gaku, who could do nothing about it. The matter was resolved at 8:00 PM that evening. As a result, the antiquities were transported from Qingdao at 7:10 AM on the 14th and arrived at Jinan Station at 7:13 PM that day. Just as they were about to be transported, there was a sudden thunderstorm, so they were placed on the platform under the watch of the railway police. This morning (the 15th) at 8:00 AM, Pi Songyun, the Section Chief of the Department of Education, and Wang Xiantang, the Director of the Provincial Library, accompanied Wu Jingshou to the Jiaoji Railway Station and directed the use of cars to transport them to the library. It was decided to inspect them again in the afternoon. An exhibition will be held in the library within the day to make them publicly viewable, to arouse public interest and attention in the preservation of antiquities. It has been verified that the bricks and tiles consist of seven boxes, about 530 pieces, and the stone tablets consist of two boxes, a total of five pieces. (June 15th)

Third Sheet

Banditry in Southern Shandong's Meng Mountain Resurges 26

Jinan Dispatch: When the bandit gang of Guo Mafeng in Baodu Mountain, Southern Shandong, was defeated, only about 700 bandits remained. Now, scattered bandit gangs such as those of Yin Tuxi and Yin Tugui have suddenly gathered again in Meng Mountain and occupied the areas around Bailingyan, Jiunuguan, Niulan Village, and Zhang Village. Their arrogance is gradually increasing. The troops of Tang Yaoxun, the Southern Shandong Militia Army, and the troops of Chen Yaohan have planned a joint suppression. Currently, Tang Yaoxun has come to Jinan from Qufu to report the latest situation of the bandit suppression to Han Fuqu. According to Tang's statement to reporters, the bandit gangs of Guo Mafeng, Yin Shixi, and Yin Shigui in Meng Mountain total more than 1,000 people, occupying the mountains. They avoid the troops when they come, and return when they leave. It is quite troublesome to suppress them. The Kong Xianfang regiment stationed in Si County is currently patrolling back and forth to prevent other defections. My visit to Jinan this time is to ask Chairman Han for heavy artillery to bombard them and to request permission to transfer the entire brigade to completely wipe out the bandits. Wang Wanqing, the Commander-in-Chief of the Southern Shandong Militia, also talked about the bandit situation in Meng Mountain, saying that when the bandits first fled from Nanshan, there were only seven or eight hundred people, but now, after gathering the forces of Yin Shigui, Li Doujin, and Li Douyin, they have reached more than 2,000 people. Lu Lianzhang's First Battalion and Liu Jianming's Second Battalion of the Southern Shandong Militia are currently assisting Tang's brigade in suppressing the scattered bandits in Meng. The headquarters of the militia was previously ordered by the Chairman to move to Pingyi Town to be responsible for the suppression in the seven counties of Fei, Si, Meng, Lin, Zou, Teng, and Yi. However, active suppression has not yet been effective. This time, coming to Jinan, I have discussed proper measures with Chairman Han and will return to Pingyi tomorrow to defend and implement them.

The Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior Jointly Establish a Film Censorship Committee 28

Censorship Will Begin on the 16th

Films in Concessions Must Also Be Censored

And Issue Orders to Unify Censorship Administration

The Film Censorship Committee jointly established by the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior will begin censorship on the 16th of this month. In order to fundamentally eliminate bad films, all films shown in concessions must also be censored in accordance with the law. This matter has been submitted by the Film Censorship Committee through the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, and consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which has notified various diplomatic missions, stating: "According to the Film Censorship Committee's report, since the establishment of this committee, all preparations have been completed and it will soon begin to censor films in various provinces and cities. However, Article 1 of the Film Censorship Law promulgated by the central government on November 3, 1930 stipulates that all films, whether domestic or foreign, must not be shown unless they have been censored by this committee in accordance with the law. Therefore, there is no doubt that both Chinese and foreign films must be censored. However, there are many theaters in ordinary provinces and cities, and there are also many in various concessions. Now, in order to thoroughly enforce the law and carry out censorship, this committee intends to uniformly censor films shown in concessions. If anyone shows films that have not been censored and approved and do not have a permit to show them, they will be severely punished once discovered, so that bad films from China and foreign countries can be eliminated in our country. Therefore, we are preparing a document to request consultation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to notify diplomatic missions that all Chinese and foreign films shown in concessions must first be censored and approved by this committee. If they do not have a permit to show them issued by this committee, they will be prohibited from showing them without authorization. Based on this, the matters reported by the committee are intended to fundamentally eliminate bad films, which is feasible. In addition to the instructions, we are enclosing 30 copies each of the Film Censorship Law and the Implementing Regulations of the Film Censorship Law for your review and notification to various diplomatic missions."

The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education jointly ordered the Departments of Civil Affairs and Education of various provinces, the Weihaiwei Management Office, and the Social Education Bureaus of Nanjing and other five cities, stating: "We have received Instruction No. 528 from the Executive Yuan, which states: 'We hereby issue an order for action. The Implementing Regulations of the Film Censorship Law and the Organizational Regulations of the Film Censorship Committee have now been formulated, promulgated, and implemented by this Yuan. In addition to issuing separate instructions, we are hereby enclosing the original provisions for your information and to instruct your subordinates to be informed accordingly. This order, etc.' We have also received a copy of the aforementioned regulations and articles of association. We hereby instruct that the Film Censorship Committee has now been formally established (affiliated to the Ministry of Education). In order to unify censorship administration, all existing film censorship agencies in various places should cease their duties from the date of receipt of this document. The educational authorities in various places should also, in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Implementing Regulations of the Film Censorship Law, clearly list the names and positions of the appointed censors (one to five persons), along with two 2.5-inch headshots of each person, and send them directly to the Film Censorship Committee to obtain a censorship certificate. Before receiving the censorship certificate, please continue to carry out censorship as before. In view of the foregoing, in addition to issuing separate orders, we are hereby enclosing the original text of the aforementioned regulations and articles of association for your departments to comply with and to instruct your subordinates to comply with accordingly."

Ni Daolang Engages in Activities in Bengbu 29

Bengbu Dispatch: Ni Sichong's private property in Anhui was confiscated and nationalized when the Northern Expeditionary Army first arrived in Anhui. Some time ago, Ni Sichong's son, Daojie, invoked the amnesty decree and submitted a request to the National Government to return his private property in Anhui, but it was not approved. Recently, Ni Sichong's nephew, Daolang, has come forward to lobby for its return. However, many people in Anhui are opposed to it. A few days ago, Daolang secretly came to Bengbu and secretly contacted former gentry in an attempt to sell the private property in Bengbu that had already been confiscated. It is said that the pre-determined selling price of the real estate is 1.6 million yuan, with the intention of reporting a donation of several tens of thousands to a certain important person in Anhui Province. The local district party department believes that Ni Daolang was one of the four great henchmen of Ni Sichong's era and a major criminal in the Jiang Gaoqi massacre. Recently, he secretly came to Bengbu to conspire to sell the seized property. Therefore, a special telegram was sent to denounce him, calling for his expulsion from the country and preventing the return of Ni Sichong's private property. (June 15th)

Water Police Suppress Bandits and Rescue Hostages: Fan Guozhong, captain of the first water police unit, recently learned of a large gang of bandits gathering and kidnapping people in the Songjiang-Qingpu border area. On the 10th, Fan personally led deputy captains Gong Guozhen and patrol officer Yao Yuangeng, each commanding a police boat, to Fengjing. They discovered that the bandits were in the Bailongtan area of Qingpu, taking advantage of the surrounding reeds, making it difficult to search. Suzhou

Progress in Establishing County Courts: The High Court has decided to first establish the Steel Mountain Higher Third Branch Court and the Changshu and Taixing County Courts, starting in the 20th year of the Republic. Additionally, the Qingjiangpu Higher First Branch Court will be able to hear first-instance cases from the 20th year of the Republic. Other judicial systems may also undergo changes.

Resolution of the Zhao Black Fish Stolen Goods Appeal: Zhao Black Fish (also known as Yang Chunbei), a Taihu pirate, had previously colluded to kidnap Xiong Tongxing's duck business in Nantian, stealing over 2,100 silver dollars. He was later arrested in Shanghai by Xu Fengshan, a detective from the Third Water Public Security District, who recovered 2,130.08 silver dollars. Zhao was extradited back to Suzhou and tried by the Wuxian District Court, which sentenced him to six life sentences, with one life sentence to be served. Zhao Black Fish appealed the decision to the High Court, which ruled on April 11 of this year to reduce the sentence to two life sentences, combined into one life sentence to be served. Zhao Black Fish still disagreed and is now appealing to the Supreme Court. After the case was solved, the victim, Xiong Ruqing, learned that Zhao Black Fish's stolen silver dollars were being held at the Wuxian District Court. Last year, he filed a civil lawsuit with the Wuxian District Court, requesting the return of the stolen silver dollars. The court ruled in his favor. Zhao Black Fish appealed this decision to the High Court. Yesterday (the 16th), Judge Zheng Zhiguo of the Civil First Chamber of the High Court convened a hearing. Zhao Black Fish claimed that 1,800 silver dollars belonged to Zhao Guilin and that he only had 330.08 silver dollars. Judge Zheng then persuaded both parties to reconcile. As a result, Xiong Ruqing was allowed to claim Zhao Guilin's 1,800 silver dollars, while Zhao Black Fish was allowed to claim the remaining 330.08 silver dollars.

Suzhou Women's School Schedules Takeover of Warehouses: Suzhou Women's School had a dispute with the Warehouse Committee over the possession of Baosu Bureau warehouse buildings. The provincial government ordered the county government to convene both parties for reconciliation, allowing the Suzhou Women's School to take possession of the buildings for school construction. However, the handover had not yet been completed. Yesterday (the 16th), the county government convened both parties for mediation again. As a result, both parties agreed to carry out the handover on the 20th of this month.

Wuxi

Appeal for Increased Ratio of Public Sale of Alcohol: The public sale fee for tobacco and alcohol in Wuxi was initially only 30,000 yuan per year. Since the adoption of a bidding system in the 17th year of the Republic, competition has arisen, resulting in Bao Pu winning the bid with a maximum amount of 71,300 yuan per year, more than double the original ratio. Various liquor merchants have repeatedly appealed, but the ratio has not been reduced. Recently, the Ministry of Finance decided to change the organization and collection method. Unexpectedly, someone named Yu and others increased the bid significantly, to over 90,000 yuan per year, and their application was approved. Upon hearing this news, the soy sauce and liquor industry association urgently convened a temporary meeting to discuss solutions. They generally believed that the public sale fee in the area had increased by more than double in one year due to speculation and competition, which was significantly different from neighboring counties. If the ratio were to be increased again, it would be too difficult to bear. After unanimous discussion, they decided to send a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce to telegraph the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau, requesting that the changes in organization and collection method be clearly announced in advance. They also requested that the approval of the increased ratio be temporarily suspended. At the same time, they appointed Qing Junqian, Tao Guanru, and others to go to Beijing to petition the ministry and bureaus.

Robbery of Two Families in Tangtou Town: In Ren Lane, Tangtou Town (Tianshang City), in the fifth district of the county, the home of Ren Achuan was suddenly invaded by more than ten robbers dressed in short blue shirts and pants, speaking in strange accents, each wielding a pistol and flashlight, breaking down the back door around 1:00 AM on the 15th. At that time, the Achuan family was already asleep. Hearing the alarm, his son, Jinrong, urgently climbed onto the roof and shouted for help, angering the robbers. They immediately opened fire, and a bullet pierced Jinrong's thigh, causing him to fall onto the roof. The robbers then tied Achuan's hands behind his back, forcing him to reveal the location of his silver. After searching for a long time, they stole seven silver dollars, over ten thousand copper coins, and two silver bracelets. The robbers then carried the stolen goods to the roof and arbitrarily searched the home of Ren Shifang, who lived next door. Shifang was a former village head and had some wealth, so the losses were significant. Ren Jinrong, who was injured on the roof, was taken by his father, Achuan, by boat to the city that night to be treated at the hospital. It is said that his leg bone was shattered, and he may become disabled.

Changzhou

Students Petition Against Closure of Women's Vocational School: The Wujin Education Bureau held an education administration meeting on the 14th and decided to close the Women's Vocational School. The general students would be sent to various girls' schools with comparable levels, while the specialized students would be subsidized with the original funding to continue their studies at the school that takes over the program, until the current class graduates. The school buildings would be taken back by the Education Bureau to be used as a public education center. Upon hearing the news, all the students of the school convened a meeting on the 15th and decided to send two representatives from each of the six grades to the Education Bureau, the County Party Headquarters, and the County Government to petition for its continuation. The Education Bureau and the County Government agreed to submit it for reconsideration at the next meeting. The County Party Headquarters said that this was a decision made by a majority of the committee members, and the Party Headquarters as individuals could not provide any response. As for the students' study problems, the Education Bureau would find a suitable solution for them. Only then did the representatives return to school.

Third Sheet

Special Education News

Opinions on the Trial Curriculum Standards for Shanghai Middle Schools 31

Since the promulgation of the provisional curriculum standards for junior and senior high school general courses by the Provincial Department of Education, the Shanghai Middle School under this municipality has been implementing them for a year and a half. During this period, in addition to actual implementation, teachers of each subject have held meetings to discuss them in detail multiple times. Now, the trial implementation opinions, in addition to being submitted to the Provincial Department for forwarding to the Ministry, are specifically recorded below:

(1) Regarding Subjects and Credits

A. Junior High School

1. The number of credits required for junior high school graduation should be reduced. The reason is that if the number of credits required for junior high school graduation is 186, then there are 38 hours of class per week, plus one hour for commemoration week, totaling 39 hours. Except for Saturday afternoons when no classes are scheduled, there are seven hours of class each day, which is too heavy a load and detrimental to students' physical health and extracurricular activities. The solution is to set the number of credits required for junior high school graduation at 180. 2. It is not advisable to change English to an elective in the third year of junior high school. The reason is that, given the current situation in China, English is a common and necessary tool for junior high school students, regardless of whether they continue their studies. If they only study for two years, the foundation will not be established, and even if previous efforts are not completely wasted, it will still be insufficient. English in the third year of junior high school should be a required course, with five hours per week. 3. Trigonometry should not be listed as a required course in junior high school. The reason is that junior high school mathematics should focus on algebra and geometry. Only a general understanding of trigonometry is learned, which is of no great benefit. It would be better to allocate the time for trigonometry to algebra and geometry, thereby achieving greater results. The solution is to remove trigonometry or change it to an elective, so that algebra is changed to twelve credits and geometry is changed to eleven credits. 4. History and geography credits can be reduced. The reason is that junior high school students should pay attention to history and geography, but this type of course has no experimental teaching materials that can be expanded or contracted. Moreover, most junior high school graduates continue their studies, and senior high school still has courses in Chinese history and geography and world history and geography, so the amount of history and geography in junior high school does not need to be excessive. The solution is to change Chinese history and geography to six credits each, and world history and geography to three credits each. 5. Physiology and hygiene credits can be reduced. The reason is that junior high school physiology and hygiene still tend to be focused on common sense, and this course emphasizes practice, so more attention should be paid to training. The solution is to change physiology and hygiene to three credits. 6. Mineralogy and chemistry should still be taught separately. The reason is that mineralogy and chemistry are not impossible to teach together, but in fact, chemistry teachers may not have a deep understanding of mineralogy, which inevitably makes teaching difficult. Moreover, the outline of the chemistry course includes too few mineralogy components. The solution is to teach mineralogy and chemistry separately, with two credits each. 7. Drawing, crafts, and music credits should be reduced. The reason is that junior high school students may not all be interested in drawing, crafts, and music. If there is this required course for all three academic years, the time spent is too much, and it cannot adapt to individual personalities. The solution is to change drawing, crafts, and music to electives in the third academic year. The three courses should each be set to four credits in the first two years. 8. Party and Scout activities should be given credits. The reason is that junior high school Party and Scout activities are as important as senior high school military training. Since military training is given credits, Party and Scout activities should be given credits. The reason is that junior high school Party and Scout activities are as important as senior high school military training. Since military training is given credits, Party and Scout activities should also be given credits. The solution is to set Party and Scout activities at six credits.

Based on the above opinions, the list of junior high school subjects and credits is as follows: Party Principles (12 credits), Chinese (36 credits), Foreign Language (50 credits), History (9 credits), Chinese History (6 credits), World History (3 credits), Geography (9 credits), Chinese Geography (6 credits), World Geography (3 credits), Mathematics (30 credits), Arithmetic (7 credits), Algebra (12 credits), Geometry (11 credits), Natural Science (16 credits), Zoology (3 credits), Botany (3 credits), Mineralogy (2 credits), Physics and Chemistry (4 credits each), Physiology and Hygiene (3 credits), Drawing (4 credits), Music (4 credits), Crafts (4 credits), Physical Education (9 credits), Party and Scout activities (6 credits), Elective Courses (8 credits), Emphasizing vocational subjects, Total Credits: 180.

B. Senior High School

1. The number of class hours for English in the second and third grades should be increased appropriately. The reason is that the general course is preparation for further education, and sufficient time should be given to build a good foundation in language tools. The prescribed work requirements are indeed indispensable. However, because the work requirements cover a wide range, and grammar and rhetoric are not assigned separate class hours, the total of only four hours per week, or 200 minutes, is insufficient to cover all aspects and achieve proficiency. The solution is to change English to five hours per week in the second and third grades. 2. The amount of mathematics should be reduced appropriately. The reason is that senior high school students have different interests. Some are interested in mathematics, while others are not. It is inappropriate to force everyone to be the same, as it would stifle individuality. The solution is to change analytic geometry to an elective. Since junior high school trigonometry is not listed as a required course (for reasons see previous opinion), senior high school trigonometry should be changed to four credits. If repeated parts of geometry are deleted (for reasons see opinions on teaching materials and teaching), four credits will be sufficient. 3. Chinese history credits can be reduced. The reason is that students have a considerable foundation in Chinese history after graduating from junior high school, so the pace of learning Chinese history in senior high school is very fast. Based on the experience of the past year's trial, it can be taught in one year with two hours per week. The solution is to change Chinese history to four credits. 4. Biology credits can be reduced. The reason is that biology teaching materials are very complex, but the representative method can be used, and at the same time, teaching and economy can be taken into account. There is no need for five hours per week. Based on the experience of the past two years, it can be taught in one year with four hours per week. The solution is to change biology to four credits. (1) Based on the above opinions, the list of senior high school general course subjects and credits is as follows:

Party Principles (12 credits), Chinese (24 credits), Foreign Language (30 credits), Mathematics (14 credits), Geometry (4 credits), Trigonometry (4 credits), Advanced Algebra (6 credits), Chinese History (4 credits), Foreign History (6 credits), Chinese Geography (3 credits), Foreign Geography (3 credits), Physics (8 credits), Chemistry (8 credits), Biology (6 credits), Military Training (6 credits), Physical Education (9 credits), Elective Courses (23 credits), Total Credits: 156.

(2) Regarding Teaching Materials and Teaching

A. Junior High School

1. English grammar should be taught separately from the reader in the third grade. The reason is that teaching the reader and grammar together is the newest principle, but based on experience, this method is suitable for the initial learning period, but not for higher grades. Because in the higher grades, more attention should be paid to the systematic aspect, and students also have this requirement and are dissatisfied with fragmented knowledge. Therefore, mixed teaching rarely achieves results in higher grades. Furthermore, from the perspective of the textbook, the textbooks compiled on the market today only add a little explanation of grammar at the end of each article, which in turn makes students' knowledge of grammar vague. The solution is that in the third grade of junior high school, there should be two hours per week dedicated to English grammar teaching, and the teaching should be linked to the reader at any time. 2. Junior high school history teaching materials should adopt the reverse narrative method. The reason is that teaching history teaching materials sequentially based on the era is sufficient to obtain an accurate sense of time, clarify concepts, and understand the signs of group evolution, but ancient historical facts are too far removed from life, and beginners easily feel bored. Because of the lack of interest, it is difficult to realize automatic research. If we start from the near and go to the far, and take a certain question for in-depth discussion, we can not only understand the origin of the evolution of historical sites, but also cultivate keen observation, thinking, and reasoning skills. The solution is to list the teaching materials in reverse order, starting with the modern, then the modern, the medieval, and the ancient, according to the teaching material outline. For example, when talking about the Chinese nation, first clarify the constituent elements of the Chinese nation and its position in the world, then the contact, growth, and assimilation of various ethnic groups, and then the origin of the nation, etc. 3. Junior high school geography teaching materials should first list the outlines of natural regionalization and political regionalization. The reason is that adopting the provincial method (or regional method) for teaching domestic geography and the country method for teaching foreign geography is rigid and impractical. However, common maps and various statistical materials cannot break the old concepts of provincial and national divisions. Moreover, to explain the location of a place clearly and accurately, regional explanations are indispensable. The application of natural regionalization or political regionalization is as necessary as latitude and longitude. Therefore, it is appropriate to first list a simple narrative to clarify the outline of all human-land relationships. The solution is to add a simple description of regionalization to the teaching material outline, and briefly describe the evolution of regionalization, the comparison of natural regions and political regions, etc., as the basis for describing natural and human phenomena.

B. Senior High School

1. English grammar should be taught separately from the reader. The reason is detailed in item 1 of section A, Junior High School. The solution is that there should be one or two hours in the first and second grades dedicated to teaching grammar. The teaching should be linked to the reader at any time. 2. Repeated parts of high school algebra and geometry and elementary algebra and elementary geometry should be deleted. The reason is that time is not economical and it hinders the higher parts. The solution is to list elementary algebra or elementary geometry formulas and theorems at the beginning of the compilation method of ordinary higher algebra, without explanation or proof, for reference. 3. Senior high school trigonometry teaching materials should be further enriched. The reason is that junior high school trigonometry teaching materials are very simple, or there is no trigonometry course at all, which seems insufficient for those who want to enter the science and engineering departments of universities in the future. The solution is to add trigonometric equations and other advanced parts in the second half. 4. High school analytic geometry should add an overview of solid analytic geometry. The reason is that junior high school only has elementary plane geometry, and high school only has a brief overview of elementary solid geometry. Students' understanding of three-dimensional concepts seems weak, which will hinder future research in advanced mathematics and physics and the drawing of mechanical drawings. Therefore, it is necessary to review solid geometry again using analytical methods. The solution is to add a chapter or two of solid analytic geometry overview after plane analytic geometry. 5. Senior high school geography courses should add natural teaching materials. The reason is that geography teaching materials focus on human aspects, but the natural environment is the basis of human phenomena, which cannot be ignored. The part about natural aspects in junior high school teaching materials is too simple and insufficient for problem research. Moreover, natural science relies heavily on geographical explanation, so there should be sufficient preparation in this course. The solution is to add several questions about natural geography to the outline of teaching materials in the domestic and foreign parts, accounting for about 20% or 30% of the total teaching materials.

(3) Regarding Grouping

The general course should still be divided into arts and science groups. The reason is that the curriculum should take into account students' interests, which is one of the principles of curriculum design. In fact, high school students' interests are close to literature and science. It is inappropriate to force them to be the same, and it is not appropriate for both teachers and students to feel difficulty. If it is said that the new school system curriculum standards set by the National Education Federation in 1923 are inadequate, only the drawbacks of elective courses can be corrected, and the principle of grouping does not need to be broken. Whether it is appropriate to adopt the training doctrine is still a question. The solution is to not group in the first grade, and from the second grade onwards, still divide into arts and science groups, restrict elective courses, and form a systematic arrangement to avoid the drawbacks of general elective courses.

(4) Regarding the Connection with Universities

The university entrance examination should be based on the middle school curriculum. The reason is that the middle school entrance examination standards should be connected with the primary school graduation level, and the university entrance examination standards should also be connected with the middle school graduation level. Only in this way can the drawbacks of separation be avoided. But in fact, the university entrance examination only considers from the university's own perspective, arbitrarily raising the level, and the standards set by each university are also inconsistent. Even comparing the entrance examination questions of the School of Science of Central University and the entrance examination questions of Jiaotong University, the levels are quite different. This chaotic phenomenon makes middle schools feel difficult. Now that there are Ministry-issued middle school curriculum standards, universities should be consistent and use this as a basis. The solution is for the Ministry of Education to issue a notice to all universities that future entrance examinations should be based on the Ministry-issued middle school curriculum standards to facilitate connection.
