Zhang Qun Returns to Shanghai Yesterday Morning 50

Talks About the Recent Situation

Shanghai Mayor Zhang Yuejun, who previously went north on behalf of the Central Government to offer condolences for Deputy Commander Zhang's illness, returned to Beijing on the 14th to report on his mission. Yesterday morning, Zhang returned to Shanghai. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed him at the municipal government, inquiring about the situation in Guangdong and the North. According to his conversation:

Deputy Commander's Illness: Deputy Commander Zhang felt unwell upon returning north and saw an increase in symptoms. Initially, he was only treated by the doctor accompanying the deputy commander. However, on the 30th of last month, he was moved to the hospital. The highest temperature reached 39 degrees Celsius. When I left Ping on the 12th, the temperature was the same as a normal person's, and his mind was also very clear. However, because his vitality had not recovered, he still needed recuperation. He may be discharged from the hospital in about a week, but after being discharged, he will either return to Shenyang for recuperation or choose another secluded place. It has not yet been determined. In short, Deputy Commander's illness has not been in any danger from beginning to end.

Situation in the North: Since Deputy Commander Zhang's illness in the North, all administrative and security matters have been maintained by various officials. Therefore, the Pingjin area is exceptionally peaceful. At the same time, Deputy Commander Zhang and others expressed absolute support for the telegraph issued by Chairman Chiang. Various rumors from the outside world, such as how a certain faction is active or that Shi Yousan's troops have different trends, are all inaccurate. The recent troop movements of the Northeast Army are entirely to support the Central Government and prevent local actions. Outside rumors are nothing more than unfounded speculation. Deputy Commander Zhang is extremely obedient to and supportive of the Central Government.

Recent Situation in Guangdong: Regarding the Guangdong issue, when I met Mr. Zhang Puquan in Beijing, he said that he had met with various important figures in Guangdong during his time there. According to what each person indicated, most advocated for a political solution. As for the Central Government, it has never expressed the use of force against Guangdong or any military action but has always advocated for a peaceful resolution. The Central Government is still primarily focused on persuasion regarding the Guangdong issue, and perhaps another path to a political solution can be found in the future.

Suppressing Bandits: The Central Government is determined to suppress the Red bandits to eliminate the major threat. At the same time, it has ample preparations in military, political, and financial matters. Sichuan has also dispatched troops to assist the Central Government in suppressing the bandits. Commander-in-Chief Chiang will probably depart within days and proceed according to the planned bandit suppression plan. Although the communist bandits are extremely rampant, it may not be difficult to annihilate them in one fell swoop.

Municipal Government Reorganization: Mayor Zhang continued to discuss the reorganization of the municipal government. He said that since the National Government announced the new organizational law of the municipal government, the detailed organizational rules of this city have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and are scheduled to take effect on July 1. There will be no changes to the departments and personnel of the municipal government after the reorganization in the future.

Staff Transfers: He also said that Municipal Government Counselor Xi Dingmo, after being appointed by the Ministry of Communications as the Shanghai Maritime Administration Director, came to the municipal government to resign this afternoon (16th). I have approved it, and his vacancy will be filled by Municipal Government Secretary Zhou Liangcai.

Domestic Goods Bazaar Unwilling to Open Automatically 51

The Municipal Council's Persuasion to Resume Business Fails

The Result Must Await Today's Negotiations

The China National Products United Bazaar has been closed for eight days after being ordered to shut down by the Municipal Council. The Municipal Council has allowed the business to resume, but the bazaar is unwilling to open automatically. Party and government agencies are preparing to discuss solutions within days. The bazaar's negotiation committee is scheduled to meet today to discuss the matter. The situation yesterday is recorded separately as follows:

Ministry of Industry Takes Action: The Industrial and Commercial Visiting Bureau of the Ministry of Industry sent personnel to negotiate with Mr. Fessenden, the Director-General of the Municipal Council. As a result, the bazaar was allowed to resume business. However, after the resumption of business, the equipment in the amusement department must be improved. Later, because the bazaar was unwilling to open automatically, the negotiation process was reported to the ministry by telegram yesterday and consulted with Zhao Tiezhang, the section chief of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office, preparing to consult with representatives from the municipal government, the municipal chamber of commerce, the municipal party department, and the social affairs bureau to discuss solutions within the possible scope.

Municipal Government Negotiations: Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, sent a letter to Mr. Fessenden, Director-General of the Municipal Council, to lodge a serious protest. The original letter is recorded below: To Mr. Fessenden: It was reported yesterday by the China National Products United Bazaar that at 3:00 PM on June 9th, the public concession police suddenly dispatched many Chinese and Western officers, armed and went to the bazaar, closing all the gates and ordering it to shut down. According to the established precedent of Wing On, an amusement department was added upstairs in order to develop the business. However, the Municipal Council created various difficulties regarding the license for the amusement department. Afterwards, a seven-year contract was signed with the landlord. How could the Municipal Council refuse to issue a license, claiming that the building was not suitable for running a bazaar, when it was requested for license application and renovation? As a last resort, they moved to No. 4 Jing'an Temple Road on May 5, thinking that the New World amusement park was a place for entertainment, and all the equipment should comply with the regulations of the bureau, and there would be no more objections. However, after the move, difficulties continued as before. Otherwise, why would the same amusement park, before the bazaar moved, when the New World was running, never have been ordered to do so? Since the venue is located in the concession, they had no choice but to obey the orders and comply with them. Unexpectedly, on June 9th, there was another move to close the entire venue and order it to shut down. The excuse was nothing more than the license issue. However, since the bazaar has no need to obtain a license and there are no violations, why was it also closed? Furthermore, the bazaar staff were illegally beaten and injured by the police and arrested and detained. All the injured persons have reported to the Special District Court to verify the injuries. Please find a way to negotiate. According to this, the Social Affairs Bureau investigated the whole matter and reported it back, which is roughly the same as the previous situation. It is difficult to understand that your Municipal Council suddenly ordered the entire bazaar to shut down and closed it because of the license issue of the amusement department attached to the bazaar. Moreover, it did not request permission from the court in advance and executed the closure rashly, which was a fundamental mistake. This measure not only hinders our national legal rights but also violates the agreement on the Chinese courts in the Shanghai Public Concession. If it is not corrected urgently, it will make the residents of the Special District feel that they cannot enjoy legal protection. Who will be responsible if a misunderstanding occurs? According to the previous report, in addition to the losses suffered by the bazaar, which should be directly requested for relief according to law by the bazaar, a serious protest is hereby lodged. Please investigate and reply. Respectfully, to Mr. Fessenden, Director-General of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council.

Wu Jingxiong's Letter: Mr. Wu Jingxiong, a municipal councilor of the Municipal Council, replied to the letter from the Manufacturers' Federation yesterday, saying: To all gentlemen of the Manufacturers' Federation of the National Products United Bazaar, I have received your letter and fully understood everything. I have been entrusted to uphold justice in this closure of the bazaar, which is related to the public interest, and I should do my best. Xiong has always advocated for justice in serving the community, and I will still do my best in this matter to find a solution in order to reach a mutual understanding and restore the original state. I am writing to inform you of this first, and I will continue with the details later. I wish you all the best.

Resumption of Business Pending: At 11:00 AM yesterday morning, the Municipal Council specially sent Police Chief Mao Ding, along with a police officer No. 209 from the New Gate Police Station, the leader of the Fire Brigade, and six people, including an interpreter, to the bazaar in person. Mr. Dong Juesun, a negotiator from the bazaar, came out to meet them and accompanied them to inspect various places in the venue, instructing the bazaar to open for business today (16th) before 2:00 PM. The amusement department can also operate after the fire brigade approves it. First, they went to inspect the Peking Opera venue. According to them, the area of ​​this stage is too large and does not comply with the regulations. Mr. Dong replied that this stage has been performing Peking Opera for more than ten years. Even on the last day of the New World's final transfer (April 30), "Journey to the West" was still performed, with mountain and water firework scenery. Why did the Municipal Council not interfere? Mao Ding said that the license given by the Municipal Council for this stage specifies (Sing Song Stage) a singing license, not a Peking Opera license. Mr. Dong replied, but the former New World performed "Journey to the West" on this stage until April 30. The playbill was published daily, and advertisements were published in various newspapers, including Shen Bao and Xin Bao, and the police and firefighters stationed by the Municipal Council all witnessed it, and the patrolling police officers also came to the venue to observe from time to time. Now, the Municipal Council suddenly blames this venue for not complying with the regulations and ordered it to shut down, which is incomprehensible. Moreover, according to my knowledge, the stages for performing Peking Opera in various amusement parks that have been licensed by the Municipal Council cannot meet the size stipulated by the Municipal Council. Can you point to a place and go to measure it? Mao Ding said that this is not my task to come here today. My task is to order the bazaar to open today. Mr. Dong said, on June 9, the New Gate Police Station came to seal the door with only the order of the chief patrol officer, without any formal official documents. Today, there are no official documents, but they still come with orders to open the door. If someone tomorrow orders the door to be closed again with the order of the chief patrol officer or the chief director, then there will be nowhere to turn. Moreover, since the door has been closed, before it is clear who is responsible for closing the door, it is not convenient to open the door easily. Mao Ding and others wanted to open the door themselves and leave, but because the door was locked, they ordered Mr. Dong to take the key and open it. Mr. Dong said that the lock on this door was also locked by the police who sealed the door, and the key is now kept by the negotiation committee. I am afraid that no one will dare to advocate opening the door before the negotiation is resolved. Mao Ding and others had no choice but to go to the Taiping Gate on Tibet Road. Ten minutes later, Western police officer No. 209 came again, wanting to meet with Mr. Zhang Zilian, the manager of the bazaar. Since Mr. Zhang had already gone out, he asked Mr. Dong to notify him by telegram when Mr. Zhang came back so that he could come to meet him and ask him to open the door today and explain the misunderstanding.

Continued Negotiations: At 8:00 PM last night, the venue received a phone call from Mr. Hong Yanbin, saying that the chief patrol officer would visit the bazaar with two Chinese directors, Yu Qiaqing and Yuan Ludeng, at 10:00 AM today to discuss solutions. It was also learned that the National Products Bazaar Negotiation Committee, because the Municipal Council knew it was in the wrong after the Ministry of Industry's Negotiation Committee sent personnel to negotiate, allowed the National Products Bazaar to resume business. Therefore, it was decided to convene all members of the Negotiation Committee at 3:00 PM this afternoon to discuss the negotiation process. The members had many suggestions, which will be submitted for discussion at the meeting.

Assistance from All Parties: More than 100 groups, including the China National Goods Maintenance Association, the dockworkers' union, the silk reeling workers' union, and the cigarette workers' union, all issued declarations yesterday to assist the National Products Bazaar in the case of being ordered to shut down by the Municipal Council. Furthermore, groups such as the Hangzhou National Goods Factory Federation, the Penglai Market Commercial Research Association, and the Shaoxing Wine Industry Guild all telegraphed the National Government's Ministry of Industry yesterday, requesting them to uphold justice and pledging to provide backing.

Foreign Ships Seize Navigation Rights Amidst the Sichuan River Shipping Tide 52

Chinese Merchants' Shipping Association Broken by Foreign Merchants

Freight Rates Skyrocket by Twofold

In the past month, the Sichuan River shipping industry has been embroiled in a major storm due to foreign merchants seeking to monopolize the shipping industry and Chinese ships forming an alliance to counter them, with both sides exerting all their efforts. This matter has been reported in this newspaper twice. However, the turn of events was unexpected. Just as the Chinese ships were beginning to unite and cooperate with merchant guilds and labor unions, a sudden change occurred within a week. The joint organization of eight Chinese shipping companies and industrial and commercial circles has been broken by foreign merchants. This has led to a surge in freight rates and a major wave of strikes by Chinese merchants. This matter concerns the survival of Sichuan River shipping rights. The reporter went to various parties to investigate in detail as follows:

Breaking the Chinese Ship Alliance: Eight Chinese shipping companies on the Sichuan River, including China Merchants, Sanbei, Zhongxing, Shuping, Yujiang, Yongqing, and Chuanjiang, united last month with eight groups, including passenger gangs, customs declaration barge companies, and packaging machinery companies, to form a business transportation association, advocating for the transportation of national goods on national ships and refusing to load foreign ships. It was formally established on June 1. Foreign merchants learned of this matter and urgently sought to destroy it. Unable to influence Yichang, they went to Chongqing. News came yesterday that the Chongqing Business Transportation Association had been influenced by foreigners, allowing foreign merchant ships to join the association. Since June 6, this association, which had been painstakingly managed by various Chinese ships, has been completely broken by foreigners. The name of the association has already been changed to the Sino-Foreign Business Transportation Association. The Chinese people's advocacy for reclaiming Sichuan River shipping rights has also been fundamentally shattered.

Foreign Merchants Skyrocket Freight Rates: After foreign merchants devised a plan to obtain Sichuan River transportation rights, they convened a meeting on June 6 with the eight Chinese shipping companies and the eight industrial and commercial transportation groups in the association, saying that there were fewer goods and more ships on the Yichang-Chongqing route, and the freight rates for upstream and downstream had been reduced several times to the minimum limit. Cotton yarn, one piece, only costs two taels, which is not enough to cover the cost of each ship. They proposed a plan to increase freight rates, increasing the charge for each piece of cotton yarn by six taels from the 6th, an increase of two times the current rate.

Foreign Ships Oppose Reducing Voyages: Representatives of various Chinese ships also requested that, at a time when there is a shortage of goods upstream and downstream, there are more than 30 ships operating on the Sichuan River, but only eight are Chinese ships, and the rest are foreign ships. In order to maintain the momentum, voyages should be reduced, and each shipping company should not have more than two ships. Unexpectedly, this plan was opposed by various foreign merchants (because each foreign shipping company has six or seven ships or eight or nine ships), who did not allow the reduction of ships, but only allowed limiting the loading capacity of each ship to only half the number of goods per voyage. If any private overloading is found, a heavy fine will be imposed, and private price reductions are not allowed. If cotton yarn freight rates are found to have been privately reduced by less than six yuan, the ship's operation will be suspended for one month. With the implementation of this plan, Chinese ships have entered a desperate situation.

Merchant Gangs Strike to Resist: After the meeting of the Sino-Foreign Business Transportation Association decided on and announced the plan, the merchant gangs in Sichuan were all shocked. According to this plan, Chinese ships on the Sichuan River only account for one-fourth of foreign ships and are bound by their restrictions, which has already fallen into a desperate situation. From now on, the shipping industry in Sichuan will be completely controlled by foreign ships. In the future, freight rates will inevitably continue to rise. Having just acquired transportation rights, freight rates have already increased twofold. The suffering of the Sichuan gangs in the future is unknown. Therefore, it was unanimously decided to stop transporting and loading in order to save the situation. The Sanbei Company in this city received this alarm and urgently telegraphed Chongqing, ordering the Dangyang ship to stop operating and return to Shanghai, and the China Merchants Bureau's Emei ship also stopped sailing, and a new plan was being made.

The Truth About the Yu Da Ship Collision 53

Talks with the Crew of the Yu Ji

The sinking of the British submarine Poseidon by the Yu Da, a vessel managed by the Hai Chang Yu Da Company, has been reported in this newspaper several times. Yesterday, the company's Yu Ji ship arrived in Shanghai from Yingkou. According to the personnel in charge of the ship, the responsibility for the Yu Da ship's sinking of the British warship lies entirely with the British submarine, because it was navigating in the wrong channel. On the afternoon of the 9th, when the Yu Da arrived at Chengshanjiao, it was traveling according to the correct channel, while the British warship Poseidon was approaching from the side, not emerging from the seabed. The Yu Da sounded its horn when it spotted the British warship, in accordance with regulations for mutual avoidance, and there would have been no danger. However, when the two ships were close to each other, the Yu Da suddenly veered outwards to give way, but the British warship suddenly changed direction, its hull suddenly crossing the Yu Da's path, making it impossible for the Yu Da to avoid or yield. The bow of the Yu Da crashed into the waist of the British submarine, causing the accident and its sinking. The captain and six other crew members were rescued by the Yu Da and went to the Weihaiwei Customs to report the incident. The Yu Da captain acknowledged the collision and signed a confirmation. The Poseidon captain also acknowledged at the customs that he had traveled in the wrong channel, resulting in the collision, and stated that the responsibility lay with his ship, unrelated to the Yu Da, also signing for responsibility. The Yu Da has now sailed from Yingkou and will arrive in Shanghai today, docking at the Yangjiadu China Merchants Wharf. Nine British warships are currently searching the sea where the British submarine sank for corpses and planning salvage methods.

Page 14

Labor-Management Agreement on Wage Issues at Silk Factories 55

Seeking Mutual Understanding, Proposing a Compromise

Wuxi Precedent: 57 Cents

Yesterday (the 16th) at 3 PM, the Shanghai Silk Factory Industry Association held a joint labor-management meeting to discuss the issue of female workers' wages. Attendees included representatives from the management side: Shen Huachen, Zhu Jing'an, Zhang Peishen, Dr. Shi, Zhang Yunsheng, Tang Yeqin, Xu Yunjiang, Tang Bingqian, and others; and representatives from the labor side: Xu Meiqin, Yang Gengdi, Wu Suzhen, Yuan Yunlong (representing the Special District), Zhang Jinsen, Chen Xiufu, Zhu Xizhang, Dong Xingen, Le Xiaorong (representing the Eastern District), and over twenty others. Shen Huachen was unanimously elected as chairman. Following formalities, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that the downturn in the foreign silk market has reached its peak. Overseas Japanese silk is being sold at low prices, increasingly impacting the market. Shanghai's white silk prices have plummeted, and the market sluggishness is unprecedented in the last twenty years. Last winter, the price of medium-grade silk dropped to over 700 taels, causing severe losses for factories, leading to wage reductions and factory shutdowns. Subsequently, the Social Affairs Bureau, aiming to maintain the livelihoods of workers, convened meetings between labor and management representatives, resulting in a resolution to reduce wages by 15%, from 60 cents per workday to 51 cents. An agreement was signed, stipulating that after the new silk season began on June 1st of the 20th year (i.e., this year), the issue of wage increases would be re-evaluated based on the market situation and silk prices. It was not guaranteed that wages would be restored upon expiration. Furthermore, the European and American silk markets remain sluggish. In previous years, the price of medium-grade silk was over 1,100 taels at the start of the new silk season. This year, however, there is little new silk being offered, and the price of medium-grade silk is only over 800 taels. The domestic cocoon yield is exceptionally poor. Statistics indicate that the cocoon production in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces can, at most, supply silk factories for four months of reeling. The quality of the cocoons is uneven, with more inferior cocoons than superior ones. Cocoon prices are remarkably high, reaching 100 yuan for foreign breeds in Suzhou, Wuxi, and other areas. With a shortage of raw materials and high cocoon prices, the factories are facing increasing hardship and have been forced to announce a complete shutdown. Given the current situation, even the current wage of 51 cents per workday for female workers is difficult to sustain, and there is no possibility of wage increases. The chairman appealed to the labor representatives to understand the hardships faced by the management, in the spirit of sincere labor-management cooperation. Following this, labor representative Yuan Yunlong stated that last year, due to the poor silk market, factories requested wage reductions. At the time, workers, recognizing the factories' operating losses, willingly endured the pain and expressed their utmost sincerity by accepting the 15% wage reduction agreement. In the past, factories had only increased wages by two or three cents at most, but the labor side agreed to a nine-cent reduction in one go, because management was on the verge of bankruptcy. Therefore, in the spirit of labor-management cooperation, they sincerely accepted the agreement. Once the term expired, the factories would naturally restore wages as agreed, allowing workers to maintain their livelihoods. Thus, even when the foreign silk market turned around and the silk price rose to 1,000 taels, the labor side did not object. Now that the silk price has reached over 900 taels, and the term of the wage reduction agreement signed last year has expired, the original wages should be restored as agreed to maintain the livelihoods of workers. Moreover, silk factories in Wuxi have already resumed paying the old wages from the first of this month. Therefore, the labor side is very resolute in demanding the restoration of wages and is determined to achieve this goal. It is hoped that the management will understand the suffering endured by the workers over the past seven months due to the wage reduction and will immediately follow last year's agreement to restore wages. Subsequently, female workers like Le Xiaorong stood up one after another to express the plight of the workers. Chairman Shen proposed to increase the female workers' wages to 57 cents, following the Wuxi method, as a compromise. He requested a vote, but the labor representatives believed that this matter concerned the interests of all workers, and they could not make a decision without consulting them. They would report the situation of today's meeting to all workers, seek their consent, and then request the Association to convene a large labor-management conference for a public decision. The meeting adjourned, and it was already past 7 PM.

Smooth Progress in the Registration of Factories by the China International Trade Association 68

The China International Trade Association, in order to introduce direct trade, recently started by investigating the situation of factories in various places, and specially organized factory registration and distributed investigation forms to various import and export merchants and factories related to import and export. More than 4,000 copies of the forms have been sent out, and the completed forms are being returned continuously. The most important items in the form are the products produced and the commodities operated. For the products produced, detailed information must be filled in, such as the product name, brand, quality, annual sales volume, cost, factory price of goods, and the amount that can be supplied daily, in order to notify factories and foreign merchants to contact each other based on this report when introducing direct trade. It is now heard that the factories are returning the forms with detailed information, because they are deeply aware of the pain that Chinese factories have suffered over the years, so they are able to understand the benefits of the association's direct introduction of trade, and they are happy to help each other.

Continued Notes on the Guanghua Factory Labor Dispute 69

Since the Guanghua Factory labor dispute occurred, the details have been reported in previous newspapers. The following is a report on the news from yesterday: (1) Labor support: Since the labor dispute occurred, there have not been many labor unions that have provided economic and practical assistance. Yesterday, various labor unions, such as the publishing industry, each donated 10 yuan. Labor representatives also continued to send letters of condolences. (2) Withdrawal of stationed police: After the factory reported to the Public Security Bureau that workers were arrested late at night, they were afraid of accidents, so they requested armed police officers to be stationed in the factory. However, all the workers strictly maintained order and continued to work as usual, so the armed police officers withdrew the night before. (3) Authorities mediate: The Guanghua Factory labor dispute case was handled by Zhou Funong from the Municipal Party Committee's People's Training Committee and Xu Ti from the Social Affairs Bureau. They summoned them for questioning on the 13th. It is now heard that the Social Affairs Bureau will formally mediate today.

Local News Two

A Man Dies After Jumping From a Building 70

Must Be a Kidnapped Victim

No One Inside, Only Weapons

At 4:45 PM the day before yesterday, a man about 40 years old jumped from the third-floor window at the back door of house number 2, Lane 40, Julieda Road, French Concession. He fell and was injured, unconscious. Many pedestrians gathered to watch, and there were many opinions, but the reason for the jump was unknown. No one came out of the house to see. After the patrolmen learned of the matter, they rushed to the scene and took the man to the Lujiawan police station. After the head of the police station determined that the injuries were serious, he ordered the man to be taken to the Guangci Hospital for treatment. Meanwhile, Bai Erde, a Western detective from the special agency of the French police station, together with detectives Jin Jiulin, Li Yaolong, Qian Yumin, Mao Jingen, Zhang Yuying, and Bao Tan Wang Licheng rushed to the house to investigate. They did not hear of any man dying after jumping from the building.

The furniture in the living room was ordinary wooden furniture. In the second floor room, there was an iron bed. Two pistols and thirteen bullets (one with six bullets and one with seven bullets) were found under the pillow, along with military commission documents and other documents. There were three floor mats on the third floor. From this, it can be inferred that the person who jumped from the building was probably a kidnapped victim, and the house was a bandit den. The victim took advantage of the bandit's carelessness and tried to escape by jumping from the window, resulting in the injury. The bandits saw the victim jumping from the window and escaping, and took the opportunity to escape from the front door. The head of the detective took the pistols and other items back to the police station for verification. The man died of his internal injuries not long after entering the hospital. The hospital notified the police station, and detectives were dispatched to take the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for an autopsy. After investigation, there were no relatives in Shanghai. Yesterday morning, the criminal section of the French General Police Station reported to Judge Zhu of the French Court to come to the hall to examine the body. Ascending to his official position, Zhu ordered an examination and determined that the unnamed man who had died was indeed killed by falling to escape. There were no relatives. The Tongren Fuyuan Hall will provide a coffin for burial, pending relatives to claim the body. The police station was ordered to take photos of the body for filing. The body was of medium height, with a shaved head, wearing a white undershirt, white bamboo cloth pants, white socks, and no shoes. The skin was white and clean, appearing to be a person from the literary or business world. Now, the photo of the body is attached to the front for relatives to identify the face and claim the body.

Thugs Burst into the Catholic Church and Stabbed a French Priest 71

The Old Priest in Critical Condition

A Suspect Has Been Detained

At 9:03 PM the night before last (the 15th), an old French priest, Mr. Lebiboul, also known as Lang Benren in Chinese, was suddenly stabbed in several vital areas with a sharp blade by thugs while he was sound asleep in the Dongjiadu Catholic Church. The details are recorded as follows:

Mr. Lang Benren took over the position of priest in the Dongjiadu Catholic Church after the original priest, Dean Bian, left in the 17th year of the Republic of China. Although he had white hair, he was very energetic and amiable in his interactions with people, so the parishioners and neighbors were happy to associate with him. He has been in office for three years and is now 62 years old. His bedroom is on the second floor on the left side of the church. Looking out of the window, the garden below is clearly visible. He liked it very much. Unexpectedly, that night, while he was sleeping soundly, a thug sneaked in to commit the crime. According to the rules of the church, the main door must be closed at 8:30 PM every night. The keeper will hand the key to Mr. Lang, and then turn off the lights and go to bed.

At the time of the incident, a loud shout was suddenly heard in the silent church, as if he was fighting with a robber and begging for help. It lasted for a long time before it stopped. The priest Zhang (Bingzhuo) and the servant in the church heard the sound and went upstairs, each with a flashlight, to investigate the corridor. They saw that the door of Mr. Lang's bedroom was wide open. So they turned on the lights and went inside to investigate. They only saw that the bed curtains and bedding covered Mr. Lang's sleeping body, all stained with fresh blood. There were also drops of blood on the floor, still red and warm. Mr. Lang closed his eyes tightly, leaning tiredly on the pillow, wounded and unconscious, unable to speak.

The crowd was surprised and at a loss as to what to do. Priest Zhang immediately reported to the Public Security Bureau of District One, Precinct One, and Director Xu quickly led Officer Zhang and Inspector Liao of the First District General Office to investigate. They immediately closed the main door and searched inside, not allowing anyone to enter or leave. The main door was heavily guarded.

Suddenly, traces of blood were found from the corridor outside Mr. Lang's bedroom, all the way downstairs to the iron fence on the west side of the main door of the hall. A three-inch long sharp knife, also covered in blood, was found in the garden. Director Xu believed that the perpetrator must have been hiding in the hall in advance, and dared to commit violence only when it was late at night. However, the search continued until yesterday morning, and the perpetrator was not found. The silent church still stood tall and solemnly in the prosperous area.

After Mr. Lang was injured, he was taken to Guangci Hospital in the French Concession for treatment. He had four stab wounds in the shoulders, arms, and other parts of his body. His condition was critical. If he can regain consciousness, he can still be saved. Precinct One, District One, has obtained clues and learned that Qin Wenbin (a former servant of the church) from Pudong is a major suspect. They have dispatched police to Pudong last night at 1:00 AM to arrest him in the Chuansha County.

Seizure of Firearms and Clothing at Xu Yabo's Home 72

Higher Court Division Rejects Appeal

Transferred to Songjiang for Trial

Xu Yabo, former chief of the water police district, was suspected by the incumbent chief Xu Pucheng of involvement with the executed Tai Bao Ashu and Zhu Quan Amei, etc. Chief Xu notified the relevant police station, and more than ten suspects were arrested at Xu's residence on Tongfu Road. After being sent to the Special District Court for trial, Chief Xu prepared a document requesting their transfer. The police station opposed this, intending to have the court handle the case. After repeated hearings, it was decided that Xu Yabo should be transferred to the Songjiang County government for trial, and he was to remain in police custody during the appeal period. Xu and the police station expressed dissatisfaction with this decision and filed an appeal, as reported previously. It has now been learned that Xu's appeal was rejected by the Second Jiangsu Higher Court Division the day before yesterday. Consequently, Xu is understandably anxious in prison. He notified his younger brother and secretly sent a trusted aide to his home in Minhang around 10 AM the day before yesterday, to steal the remaining firearms and clothing from his tenure. Just as they were unloading the boat, they were discovered by detectives from the First Water Police District. They reported to Chief Xu Pucheng, who immediately dispatched armed soldiers to Xu's home, where they seized two large boxes of bullets, three Mauser rifles, one pistol, and hundreds of sets of military uniforms. Xu's trusted aide, identified as Mr. Jia, was also temporarily detained at the district headquarters, pending investigation.

Apprentice Lies About Kidnapping 73

Attempting to Defraud Employer of 2,000 Yuan

An Amusing Account of the Incident

Zhongyi Hospital at No. 780 Zhejiang Road hired an apprentice named Wu Boping last month. He is a local. He suddenly went missing on the 7th of this month. Hospital owner Zhao Zhongren reported to the police station, requesting an investigation. Initially, there were no clues. Two days later, Zhao received a letter by post, which he opened and found to be from Wu. It stated that on the afternoon of the 7th, five bandits impersonated his uncle and invited him away, resulting in his imprisonment in a bandit den where he suffered greatly. He pleaded for a loan of 2,000 yuan to be delivered to No. 4 Xiafei Road on the 11th, to secure his release. After reading this, Zhao reported to the Laozha Police Station, which dispatched detective Yan Heng to investigate as scheduled. No one was found. The day before yesterday morning, Wu suddenly returned by car, dressed in tattered clothes. Zhao questioned him in detail. Wu claimed that he had indeed been kidnapped and held near Bansongyuan. He said that he managed to escape while the bandits guarding him were asleep, and that he had told the police everything he had been through. Zhao found his story suspicious and inquired of the rickshaw puller who had served Wu, who stated that he had been hired by Wu at the Great World. Thus, Wu's lies were exposed. Zhao then sent Wu to the police station for investigation. Wu could not hide the truth and confessed. He had gone to Xin Xin Company alone on the 7th and met a man named Chen Qinghe at the Daxijing performance area. He was invited to Chen's home at No. 197 Xintangjia Lane for the night. The next day, Chen instructed him to send a letter to his employer, falsely claiming that he had been kidnapped by bandits in an attempt to defraud him of 2,000 yuan. Detectives then arrested Chen Qinghe. Yesterday morning, both were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Shen Shumu presided over the trial. Wu was sentenced to three months of imprisonment, and Chen was sentenced to six months, as a warning.

Woman Eager to Die 74

Throws Herself into the Huangpu River, Luckily Rescued

Then Attempts to Run Into a Car

At around 9 AM yesterday, a woman over forty years old threw herself into the Huangpu River at the Yangjingbang Company wharf. Fortunately, Chinese police officer No. 44 from the Customs patrol happened to see it and immediately rescued her. She was taken to the police station, but she did not say a word when asked about the reason for her suicide. After a short time, she showed signs of fear and made strange noises, appearing to have a mental disorder. She remained silent for three hours, before suddenly saying, "I want to die." The police officers recognized a Ningbo accent and dispatched Detective Wu Rongsheng to send her to the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai at 2 PM. After getting into a rickshaw, she saw a car approaching and jumped out, attempting to collide with it. Fortunately, Detective Wu got out of the rickshaw immediately and stopped her, preventing an accident. The detective then kept a closer eye on her along the way, and she arrived safely at the association.

Three Deaths in Western Shanghai 75

Crushed to Death... Drowned... Electrocuted

The area west of Shanghai, including Caojiadu, Zhoujiaqiao, Xiaoshadu, and the Tanzigou Zhongshan Road area, is vast, remote, and sparsely populated, with a mix of people from all walks of life. The police force is limited, making it difficult to effectively maintain order. Fortunately, Chief Ren of the Sixth District has implemented strict security measures at various key points, so cases of theft have been rare recently. However, in the past week, several incidents of murder, being crushed to death, and electrocution have occurred in various parts of the Sixth District, resulting in the deaths of nine people, which is unusual. These include: (1) On the 9th of this month, farmer Hong Renzheng from the Xu Family Residence on Zhongshan Road was shot and killed. (2) On the same day, an unidentified male corpse was found in the small creek inside the culvert at No. 23 Zhongshan Road, also shot and killed. (3) On the 10th of this month, Jiang Yipin, a worker at the Rihua Yarn Factory on Laobesheng Road, fell from an elevator and died. (4) On the 11th of this month, an unidentified male corpse, strangled to death, was found in the small creek inside the culvert at No. 25 Zhongshan Road. (5) On the same day, five-year-old Cao Jingen from Dingjiaku was crushed to death by a cargo truck. (6) The day before yesterday, an unidentified male corpse, stabbed to death in four places, was found behind the Xiaoshadu Tanbei Lime Mill. The above six cases have already been detailed in this newspaper. The following is a report of the three cases that occurred the day before yesterday:

Woman Crushed to Death by Train: At around 8:30 PM the day before yesterday, Ms. Yu Zhu, a 25-year-old woman residing in the Caoguonei area of the Xiaoshadu Lime Mill in western Shanghai, had a quarrel with her husband, Yu Tonggan. In a fit of anger, she ran out alone. While attempting to cross the tracks at the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway near Wangjia Lane in Tanbei, due to the dimness of the evening and being disoriented, she was struck by a train traveling from Shanghai to Hangzhou. She was knocked down by the train and her head and legs were crushed, resulting in instant death. Her father, Yu Rongxiang, and her son, Yu Tonggan, inspected the body the night before last. The corpse was a bloody mess, a horrific sight. They immediately reported the incident to the Sixth District Police Station, which instructed the local bailiff to report to the court for an inspection.

Male Corpse in Small Creek: At around 7:25 PM the day before yesterday, a male corpse suddenly floated up in the small creek behind the Shenxin Yarn Factory in Zhoujiaqiao in western Shanghai. Someone spotted it and reported it to the Second Sub-Station of the Sixth District. Officer Wei went to investigate and found that the corpse was completely naked, around twenty years old, and appeared to be a worker. According to nearby residents, someone was seen swimming in the creek at around 4 PM that afternoon. It is believed that they drowned due to the hot weather and lack of swimming skills. The police were instructed to investigate and notify the family of the deceased for further investigation.

Electrician's Apprentice Electrocuted: Wu Jisan, an apprentice floor sweeper, around 20 years old from Shandong, was sweeping up dirt in the cloth weaving room of the Shenxin Yarn Factory in Zhoujiaqiao in western Shanghai at around 4:10 AM the day before yesterday. He accidentally touched a wire, causing him to be electrocuted and fall to the ground. He was numb all over. Workers saw this and immediately tried to rescue him, but it was too late. He died instantly. The factory notified his family, who came and took the body back for burial.

Patron Turns Assassin 76

Prostitute Only Cares About Money

Old Hubei Feels Betrayed, Kills Lover

In the Zhide Lane, No. 8 Zilaihuo Street, French Concession, is a brothel run by a madam from Jiangxi. One of the prostitutes, Jin Ying, is 22 years old and from Jiangxi. She is of average appearance, and her business is not bad. Last month, Jin received a patron nicknamed Old Hubei, who stayed with her for over a month, spending over a thousand yuan. Recently, his money ran out, and Jin became increasingly cold towards him. The madam also demanded that he pay before staying. Yesterday (the 16th), at around 3 AM, Jin had taken in a previous regular patron. Old Hubei also arrived, but Jin did not show him any affection and gave him a cold look. Old Hubei was furious and went outside to hide an eight-inch-long sharp knife, waiting outside Jin's back door (Jin usually entered and exited through the back door of Renmei Lane). Jin went out for a snack and was spotted by Old Hubei. He called Jin a heartless and ungrateful whore. Jin also responded with harsh words. Old Hubei then stabbed Jin violently in the abdomen with the knife and fled. Jin was quite strong. Although the knife was stabbed into her abdomen, she pulled it out and cried for help. Blood gushed out like a fountain, and she fell to the ground in pain. The madam rushed over and saw Jin holding her abdomen wound with one hand, blood still flowing out. She could not speak. The madam took Jin to Renji Hospital for treatment and reported the incident to the police, asking them to apprehend the murderer.

Qiu Jin's Daughter, Wang Guifen, Returns to China 78

Wang Guifen, the daughter of revolutionary heroine Qiu Jin, is the principal of the Jingxiong Women's School in this port. She studied at New York University in the United States in 1928. After graduating, she went to Washington to study aviation and obtained a doctorate. She returned to China by ship on June 3rd and arrived in port on the 21st. It is said that she has written several books on aviation, pioneering the field of aviation for women in our country.

130,000 Counterfeit Cigarettes Seized 80

"Namo Wen" Closely Resembles the "Fairy" Brand

British American Tobacco Company Believes They are Counterfeit

The "Namo Wen" brand cigarettes manufactured by the Meixing Cigarette Factory at No. 414 Taiyuan Lane, Qipu Road, are believed by the British American Tobacco Company to imitate the style of their "Fairy" brand. They reported to the Huishi Police Station, requesting an investigation. The day before yesterday, the head of the detective department dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to the Meixing Factory and seized three large boxes, totaling 138,000 cigarettes, which were deposited at the police station. Yesterday morning, Qian Xunjiu, the lawyer for the police station, sent the two brands of cigarettes to the Special District Court for instructions. Judge Shen questioned the search situation. As no responsible person was present, he instructed that the cigarettes be temporarily stored in the warehouse, pending further action.

Cantonese Opera to Open in Shanghai 81

Starring Chen Feinong, Liang Shaofeng, and Others

The Cantonese Opera New Spring Troupe, organized by famous Cantonese opera performers Chen Feinong, Liang Shaofeng, Yi Qiushui, Feng Xiaofei, etc., has been performing in Guangzhou, Hong Kong, and other places. They have been very well-received, with tickets selling for up to five yuan and still having a full house. This time, they are coming to Shanghai to perform famous operas at the Guangdong Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road, with tickets selling for only two yuan and fifty cents. As a result, the audience is extremely crowded. The female lead, Chen Feinong, is known as the "Mei Lanfang of Guangdong." She has a charming appearance, a natural singing voice, and delicate expressions. She comes from a wealthy family; her father was a high-ranking official in the Qing Dynasty. She is an amateur performer turned professional and has become increasingly proficient in her studies. Liang Shaofeng is the male lead, and his reputation is similar to that of Jiang Miaoxiang. It is said that Chen's salary for the Cantonese opera season in Shanghai is as high as 28,000 yuan per month, which shows the value of her art. The organization of Cantonese opera is very similar to that of Peking opera, but the costumes, music, and singing have their own unique spirit. The plays and lyrics are particularly elegant and worthy of recitation. It is hoped that the people of Shanghai can take the time to listen to Cantonese opera and gain new knowledge in the field of drama.

Deaths of Two Women 82

Both Due to Intolerable Abuse

Young Woman Hangs Herself: Ms. Wang, about 25 or 26 years old, dressed fashionably, was found hanging in the front building of No. 340 Taihua Lane, North Jiangxi Road, yesterday afternoon at around 5 PM. The family reported it to the Hongkou Police Station, which dispatched police to the scene and sent the body to the Tongren Hospital mortuary for examination. It is said that her husband runs a carpentry shop at the intersection of Qipu Road and Jiangxi Road and has a primary wife who lives upstairs in the shop. Ms. Wang was a concubine and committed suicide because she could not bear the abuse from the primary wife.

Young Maid Poisons Herself: Young maid Xu Yuying, 14 years old, was sold to No. 28 Dongxin Lane, Daziming Bell, French Concession. She often stole things from her employer to give to her mother. The night before last, her mistress discovered this and gave her a slight beating. Afterwards, Yuying was extremely depressed and secretly swallowed opium paste in an attempt to end her life. She was rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment, but she died at around 1 AM the next morning due to the severity of the poisoning.

General Meeting of the Machine Industry Association 83

The Shanghai National Products Machine Industry Association held its fifth first member congress at the Central Vegetable Society at 4 PM the day before yesterday. More than 100 representatives from various member factories attended. Wang Hanqiang, Ye Guancheng, and Ji Jiannan were publicly elected to the presidium. After the opening ceremony and reports from various departments, elections were held. As the number of votes cast did not exceed half, the ballots were sealed by the vote counters Zhu Zhenhan and others. Members who had not voted were notified to vote quickly before another meeting could be held to reveal the results. Three member proposals were tentatively resolved but were reserved for formal passage at the next meeting. The association has been making unremitting efforts to promote the standardization of weights and measures. Yesterday, in addition to distributing a copy of "A Brief Explanation of Weights and Measures" and a ruler to each person, the walls of the venue were covered with diagrams and tables on weights and measures, such as "Crimes of Counterfeiting Weights and Measures," "A Brief Summary of the Promotion of Weights and Measures," "Explanation of Platinum and Iridium," and the purpose and distinction between the metric and market systems. Members participated in a weights and measures game, weighing themselves with standard market coins and other weights. Xu Yunnan was the heaviest, Shen Pengcheng was the lightest, and Yang Xiaoan was closest to the average weight. Each was given a white hat and a large cake to add to the fun.

News from Labor Unions 91

It was resolved to send Zhou Lianlin to negotiate. The factory agreed to pay on his behalf.

The discussions included: (1) The Social Affairs Bureau is collecting the old industry regulations of various industries and requesting a copy of the approval documents that were submitted to the government for filing. It was resolved to hand it over to the document section for handling. (2) No funds to be raised quickly responded, (3) Jiangxi disaster relief fundraising, decided to team up, (4) Municipal Chamber of Commerce distributed the rules and details of awards for small industry and handicraft industry, decided to inform the members (5) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce annual fee urgently needs to be paid, how should it be handled, the meeting resolved to collect monthly fees, in order to facilitate payment.

The Fei Tang Second Volume Report 94

Summary Translation of the Fourth and Fifth Sections

Note: The Second Volume Report includes the Fourth and Fifth Sections of this report. This summary mainly extracts and summarizes the key content of the Fifth Section, discussing "Key Issues Concerning the Future of the Public Concession." Regarding the content of the Fourth Section, apart from the quoted sections in the final chapter, the rest is only briefly described. For brevity, many important arguments in the original book have been omitted. For detailed information, please refer to the full text of the report. The original text of the Second Volume Report can be purchased directly from Kelly & Walsh, China American Publishing Company, and Evans & Sons Limited, priced at two dollars and fifty cents each. The Chinese translation is in progress.

The report is divided into seven sections as follows: Section 1, Introduction; Section 2, History and Status of the Public Concession and Its Governance System; Section 3, Shanghai Business Interests; Section 4, Statements Received Regarding Political and Administrative Issues and Their Comments; Section 5, Key Issues Concerning the Future of the Public Concession; Section 6, Outside Road Surface; Section 7, Addendum. The first three sections of the report have already been published. What is now being published is the report of the Fourth and Fifth Sections.

The letter from Mr. Fei Tang to the Chairman of the Municipal Council on June 15th has been summarized and published at the beginning of the Second Volume Report as a preface, as follows: "I firmly believe that readers of this report will remember the full responsibility for the content of the report, as mentioned in my letter to your Chairman on April 23rd, which served as the preface to the first volume of the report, rests solely with me and is unrelated to any other individuals, as well as my desired attitude of readers of this report. One thing I have paid attention to is the comment published in a certain Chinese weekly newspaper on May 14th regarding the first volume of the report, which stated, 'The entire report is divided into two volumes and has not yet been sold, but it has long been archived and has been submitted to the British government for approval before publication.' This rumor is completely inaccurate. When the first volume of the report was published on April 25th, the currently published second volume was still being compiled and was far from completion. No part of this report has ever been submitted to the British government or any other government for approval at any time. The report stated that on April 27th, British Foreign Secretary Mr. Henderson mentioned in the House of Commons in response to a question that 'this report has been seen.' It is speculated that this answer refers to the chapters in the first volume, as I had sent the proofs of each chapter to London in advance so that the London press could also receive them on the day of publication here. These proofs were indeed delivered to London on April 20th, five days before publication here. Mr. Henderson's answer on April 27th, stating that 'the report has been seen,' must refer to these chapters. Mr. Henderson could not have seen other chapters, nor were there other chapters available for Mr. Henderson to read. If this answer is taken seriously and becomes the basis of the aforementioned rumor, it is a complete misunderstanding. The reason I mention this rumor is because someone told me that if it is not corrected, it may cause misunderstandings and harmful consequences in certain aspects. Readers of this volume may not have seen the first volume, so I believe that the letter from me to the Chairman of the Municipal Council on April 23, 1931, which was published in the first volume of the report as a preface, should be summarized and reprinted as follows: 'The Municipal Council, especially me, has conducted a free investigation entirely in accordance with the law, and at the same time, has gladly provided assistance to my request, for which I am deeply grateful. The assistance of the Council members and staff is extremely valuable. I have found the assistance of these people to be the same as the assistance of the majority of people outside the Council who have nothing to do with Council affairs. The topics I should pay attention to and the sources I should ask are entirely up to me to decide freely. After the materials are collected, I am free to process and judge them in accordance with the law. The full responsibility for the content of the report, therefore, rests solely with me. Only I am bound by the chapters in this volume and the volumes that will continue to be published, and no one else. Regarding the attitude of readers of my report, I would like to briefly state my wishes as follows: Those who are familiar with the situation in Shanghai, regarding the problems that I have been entrusted to deal with, will recognize its difficulty and complexity. My requests for assistance have been readily granted, mostly due to deep sympathy for the difficulty of my duties. Regarding the facts of this difficulty, it may allow me to make a request to the reader, whether they are in Shanghai or not. I would like to ask all readers to listen patiently so that I can finish my words, and when reading the report, not only be patient but also have an open mind. When preparing the report, I deeply felt that the greatest service I could hope to provide to all citizens of the Public Concession, to the best of my ability, was to make a fair and unbiased account of the main facts regarding the situation in the Concession. This account must include all issues that have been fiercely disputed in the past or present, and when conducting a fair study of these issues in their true light, there may be remarks that are not welcomed by one party or another. Part of what is said may not be accepted by a portion of foreigners' opinions, and another part of what is said may not be accepted by a portion of Chinese opinions. I sincerely ask all parties concerned not to be resentful of what I say. If I were to offend the intentions of this party or that party, and not present the various relevant reasons that must be taken into account, then I would fail to fulfill the duties that the Municipal Council, representing all residents of the Concession, has unanimously asked me to undertake. My responsibility is very clear, that is, not only to avoid discussing the problems seen in order to make the report acceptable to the general public, but also to avoid mentioning the main reasons why this party or that party's point of view is considered unpleasant. The length of the report is inevitable, as mentioned above. I would like to specifically ask readers not to read each section separately from its context, or only hold on to a certain word or sentence, or not seek the complete meaning of the offense, and make judgments. Please read the entire report completely first."

Section 4: This section describes the statements received regarding political and administrative issues and their comments. Chapter 1 describes the detailed organization of the taxpaying Chinese. In early March 1930, the association submitted a set of questions to solicit opinions on various issues related to the administration of the Public Concession and suggestions regarding the future of the Concession. The set of questions is quoted, and a portion of the answers received by the association is reprinted. The most detailed of the answers received is the statement of the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions, which was published by the Federation itself in the newspaper. Five other simpler answers from various guilds are also quoted. Comments on the arguments raised in each answer have mostly been made in later chapters. What is noted here is that although all answers advocate the recovery of the Public Concession, and some advocate immediate recovery, there are two cases that advocate that a transitional period should be undergone before recovery. The relevant groups in each answer all hope to make certain modifications to the current organizational law so that the Chinese can participate more in the management of the affairs of the Public Concession, and hope that this modification can be realized before recovery. Chapter 2 describes the written statements of opinions from religious groups residing in or near the Public Concession. Certain general questions regarding the current administration of the Public Concession and its possible future plans have been submitted to each religious group for consideration. Chapter 3 describes the statement submitted by the Joint Committee of Women's Associations regarding the suppression of industrial conditions. The general comments on this statement are as follows: This statement notes a major defect in the current organizational law of the Public Concession, namely the lack of sufficient legislative power. This defect has been mentioned before and will be discussed in detail in Chapter 5. The topic specifically addressed by the Joint Committee of Women's Associations is the suppression and improvement of industrial conditions in and around the Public Concession. This topic has a great impact on the welfare of the Chinese society in the Public Concession and involves far-reaching economic issues, making it one of the most important issues for which legislative and administrative powers must be expanded. The report then describes the Child Labor Committee from 1923 to 1924. The report of the committee describes the situation of child labor in factories in and around the Public Concession, as well as the factory law promulgated by the National Government but not yet implemented. Examples are also given to indicate the drastic nature of all the provisions of the law and comments are made as follows: If the newly formulated law is immediately and fully enforced, the result will inevitably be industrial chaos, factory closures, and countless workers will lose their jobs. The source of capital for Chinese factories is often smaller than that of foreign factories, so the impact on Chinese factories will be far greater than on foreign factories. However, it is extremely important to start improving the current factory conditions, especially the improvement of child labor factory conditions. The report of the Child Labor Committee has vividly described this situation. Chapter 4 describes the resolutions on public health issues passed by the Shanghai Medical Association in March 1930 and discusses various issues regarding the public health administration of the Public Concession. What is emphasized is the opposition faced by those who promote public health in Shanghai, which is of a particularly serious nature. The reason is that the Chinese attitude is conservative, distrustful of modern medicine, and their habits and lifestyles are old-fashioned. When interfered with by civil servants responsible for implementing public health prevention methods, they strongly oppose it. The fierce situation formed in November 1910 due to the attempt to implement plague prevention is quoted in the report, and it is pointed out that although the hospitals and medical facilities provided to meet the needs of the Chinese people cannot be compared with those provided for foreigners, "as far as the general work of the Municipal Council's Health Department is concerned, not only do the Chinese obtain the majority of the benefits of the affairs handled by the department on an equal footing with foreigners, but all the work of the department has been and still is carried out for the special interests of the Chinese people, which is not a small number." Moreover, "the work done for the Chinese people is mostly done in the face of special difficulties, and even though these difficulties are encountered, valuable work has been accomplished." The health investigation team of the League of Nations came to China at the end of 1929 to conduct an investigation and prepared a statement including comments on the general situation of public health in Shanghai, and mentioning the work of the Municipal Council's Health Department of the Public Concession and the Shanghai Municipal Government's Health Bureau. The summary of this statement is also quoted in the report. The report then mentions the Hospital and Nursing Services Committee organized by the Municipal Council of the Public Concession in July 1931, but the committee has not yet submitted its report. The part of the statement submitted by the Federation of Trade Unions regarding the hospital issue is quoted as follows: The sanitary equipment in the concession is extremely incomplete for the Chinese people. For example, in the case of hospitals, although the Chinese population is over 800,000, the number of hospitals is very few, while Westerners have many conveniences. The comments on this statement are as follows: Although this statement contains some important facts, its understanding of the general situation of the Public Concession in terms of hospital facilities and medical convenience is superficial and misleading. The Municipal Council has undoubtedly provided more hospital and medical equipment for the Chinese people in and around the Concession than any Chinese municipal authority has provided for the Chinese people in its jurisdiction. The details mentioned above indicate that the Municipal Council has specially established an isolation hospital for the Chinese people, and has given annual subsidies to several other hospitals, either exclusively serving the Chinese people or allowing Chinese people who seek medical treatment to receive it together with foreigners. In addition, it must be remembered that most of the hospitals in the Public Concession that are set up for foreigners are operated by private foreigners or generously donated by foreigners. The main hospital in the Public Concession that is set up for the Chinese people was founded by foreign philanthropists, and its maintenance costs are mostly dependent on foreign donations. However, in terms of municipal expenditure, the equipment supplied to meet the needs of foreigners is indeed more complete than the equipment supplied to meet the needs of the Chinese people. The total amount of public funds in the Public Concession used to provide medical care for a small number of foreigners is indeed greater than that used to meet the needs of Chinese hospitals. This is also the actual situation. However, it must be noted that because the salaries of foreign nurses are better, the maintenance cost of hospital equipment, calculated per bed, is greater for foreign patients than for Chinese patients. The difficulties experienced by the Chinese in accepting hospital treatment and complying with its rules have been described above. Although the prejudices of the Chinese against hospital treatment are now gradually being broken down, these difficulties still exist. The equipment for supplying the medical needs of poor Chinese people seems to need to be increased. No matter what method is used, allocating municipal funds to expand this equipment will help to eliminate the current inequality in the medical convenience of hospitals and medicine provided by the Municipal Council for Chinese and foreign residents.
